repreſented view manifolde daungers perills preſently ſawe whereof forced abide euenture béeing thus perplexed god diuine goodneſſe recomforted vpon ſaturdaye fourth day nouember nine clocke forenoone haue landed howbeit know land commaunded caſt ſea boord ſo paſſed along ſame vntill tewſdaie following time came perfect viewe ſight land perceiuing ſame lye lowe great bay conuenient place ſhips ſo commanded fall anker purpoſe take water afterward named iland sanctum haelena deſcription people manner saint helen iland people countrie within ſaid iland men afterward found ſame bée lyttle men ill fauoured face colour blacke ſpeake ſuch manner though alwayes ſigh theyr apparell beaſtes ſkinnes made manner french cloakes truſte vp hide theyr member certeine caſes made woode verye well wrought haue armes weapon certaine ſtaues oke trée bathed toaſted fire endes whereof horne beaſts ſomwhat burnt hardened fire alſo ſeruing ſwoords wherewith hurt enimie theſe people doe mainteine themſelues rootes hearbes sea woulfes whale fiſh countrie hath great plentie likewiſe ſea crowes ſea mewes alſo doe eate beaſtes call gazelas doues beaſts bird haue land kéepe alſo dog thoſe ben portingale sancty ago whence whole fléete prouided themſelues freſh water next day generall captaines ſome companie went ſhore intending ſée view manner people inhabited countrie land whether coulde informe farre thence cape buena eſperansa knew neither head chiefe pilot voyage certeintie voyage wherein hée went bartholome dyas departed morning cape sea paſt ſame night forewinde firſt going came néere shore reaſon wherof know land notwithſtanding hée coniectured déemed aboue thirtie league diſtaunt thence vttermoſt generall diſimbarked come land walking ouertooke man one inhabitaunts ſame going landward ſawe thoſe ſauage people comming preſently imagined meant harme therefore foorthwith commaunded whole fléete put themſelues battaile araye himſelfe certaine others went landward without anye weapon déeming verely thoſe blacke men meant harme would offer anye force indéede ſawe boates comming ſhoreward began runne away great clamour outcrie ſo manye others alſo lay ſecretly hidden amongſt certeine buſhes policie vſed traine men rather lande diſimbarked landed returned furiouſly ſet vpon ſhooting dart vſing weapon ſuch ſort inforced men retire boates imbarke themſelues haſt taking witneſſe diſcouerie calicut ſo end ſo long time god returne v thether without ſaid would hard beléeued wée diſcouered calicut credit honour woulde ſtand ſuſpence ballance vntill ſuch time ſhould come perſons credit thence ſhoulde declare bée true affirmed therefore doe thinke yt rather die ſuffer ſo long time haue ſpent lyke ſpend others ſhall come diſcouer ye truth ſeruice ſo meane thoſe enuious ſhould iudge trauaile ſhuld pleaſe certeinly rather die tarrie vpon ſame much friend doe aduenture ſelfe ſo great daunger death ſurmiſe neither yet ſhould remaine ſo great danger doe preſuppoſe goe countrie chriſtians talke king deſirous vnto citie ſhould come many merchant profit doth ariſe thereby vnto merchant reſort vnto wil profit doe goe thether ſtay many day moore ſhall haue ſuch time vſe anye treaſon againſt ſo much doe minde talke king ſhall haue end within thrée dayes▪ time may readineſſe touching honour credit ſhall get making eſtabliſhing trade pleaſe god doe accept ſame giue treaſure king ſettle ſame better eſtéeme beare ſome reuerence towards knowen vnto captaine generall fléete king portingales embaſſadour rather perſon whatſoeuer furthermore whoſoeuer ſhall goe ſteede king thinke himſelfe mockt eſteeme one worthy ſhoulde goe ſpeake el doe truſt word beſides cannot giue ſo large inſtructions ſhould ſend thether might doe thing néedfull much ſelfe ſo ſinnes ſhoulde kill take priſoner great deale better ther ſhuld chaunce duetie remaine alyue doe ſame friendes remaining sea good ſhipsthe generall determined goe calicut ſoone ſhal heare theſe thing ſhall chaunce time yt ye captaine general came land whereas ye catual tarrieng accompanied 200 nayres attended ther continually beſids many others y• wer company beſides many alſo yt yt towne captaine generall diſimbarkedthe captaine generall goeth lād ioyfully receiued yr catuall ye others yt accompany though glad comming yt thus receiued taken andor y• king calicut ſent bring vpon yt countrey accuſtomed goe horſebacke theſe andors like vnto horſlitter ſauing yt wtout couer ouer almoſt plaine ye ſides therof alſo low theſe andors occupie ye ſame caried wt 4 men vpon ſholders alſo doth run poſt wt thē ſuch time ye king noble men make great iourny ſo yt wil go great ground ſmall time may trauell ye ſame either ſitting lieng wil themſelues alſo ther go theſe certain footman carie hat wherwith couer thoſe y• go theſe andors call bueys ſo meanes kept y• ſunne raine ther alſo andors y• haue ouer thē cane bowed like vnto hoope y• made ſlight may eaſily carie thoſe 2 men captaine generall moū ted andor departed wt catuall carried another andor town called capocate ye reſt cōpany went afoote people country cō maunded catuall carie ſuch apparel mē brought vp wt thē ther redeliuered vnto thē capocate ſtaid refreſh themſelues captaine generall one houſe catuall another eatethe fruit calicut al men giuen eat ſodden fiſh wt rice butter beſides fruit ye countrey differ much yet good one ſort theſe called lacas mangas howbeit haue fig alſo water yt drinke excellent good portingal thus eaten went againe imbark themſelues ſhuld go vp riuer thence runneth ſea captaine generall imbarke himſelfe company 2 almadias lieng one cloſe y• countrey call enſangada catuall wt traine imbarked many others people came riuers ſide ſée view men without number ſo much countrey well inhabited gone riuer league along ſhores ſide ſaw lieng ground many great ſhips captaine generall catuall diſimbarked returne andors following waye reſorted alwayes thouſandes people ſée wherein tooke ſuch felicitie beſides many others inſomuch yt great power poſſeſſions people much rich thing neceſſarie king thoſe part hath ſo ben ye ſpace theſe lx yeres ſo y• thoſe yt haue ben king predeceſſours hauing fame accompanied like going afoot ther fell ſuch raine ye ſtréets ran full therof therefore driuen cōmaund ſome men carry vpon back water y• would late euer y• could come lodging ye captaine general ſo angry y• complained vpon ye king factor demaunding whether meant carry citie ye night anſwered yt could otherwiſe yt ye city great ſcattered ſo carried owne houſe reſt himſelfe afterward gaue horſe vpon ye might ride yt horſe wt ſaddle ye captaine wold accept offer ſaieng ye yet rather wold go foot ſo went vntill ſuch time came lodging thoſe y• accompany left good lodging comming men brought haue brought golde merchaunt ambaſſadour cauſe brought none doth ſend ye king calicut good ye king maiſters certeinly know hée ſhould haue met king calicut therfore giue nothing preſent withal next according ye greatnes eſtate vnto captaine generall reply ſaieng yt good yt cuſtome ſhuld kept preſeruatiō ſame make preſent greater value cauſe aboue ſaid therefore deſired ſuffer carrie ſame king embaſſadour théefe went rob knew moſt certaine factor certified aſſoone come monſambicke wher xeque went viſite captaine generall aboord ſhippe ſent preſents eſtabliſhed friendſhip alſo giuing pilot carrie calicut whether ſaid would goe ſhot ordinaunce towne killed subiects tooke certaine sambucos laden merchaunts handeled like vnto enimies departed thence mombaſſa likewiſe vnder ye color friendſhip ſaieng bound towarde calicut king therevpon tooke occaſion ſend viſite captaine generall aboord ſhip requeſting enter harbour determined ſo doe whether ſaw within ſame many ſhips yt thought could make partie good flye away ſo faſt left one ankors behinde thence alſo pilot ran away caried monſambicle ill lyfe lead whipping putting vnto puniſhment departed mombaſſa come néere vnto mylynde take perforce sambuco laden moore ye ſome dyed battaile others yet aliue remaining captiues thoſe captiues willed carry mylynde ſaieng woulde giue newe pilot carrye calycut meanes onely came thether hauing king mylynde bene receiued well yet captaine generall would come lande fearing hurt done taking moore priſoner king ſent viſit would delyuer vntill ſuch time pilot ſent wher might well conſidered ſo embaſſadour come maintaine peace would neuer haue vſed thoſe diſorders wold haue brought king preſent demeanour giue thée vnderſtand dutie bindeth v thou maiſt doe thou ſhalt thinke good thereinthe king remaineth doubt full vvhat doe newes king remained amazed told moore would determine himſelfe ſhall thought moſt conuenient ſéeing thought ſame waye cauſe king doe would haue afterward tell catuall thereof great credite king requeſting perſwade king receiue ſuch embaſſage cauſe thereof rather tooke preſent ſo ſmall valew catuall went immediately king told moore ſaid catuall gaue counſaile doe moore requeſted immediately king began change countenaunce againſt captaine generall ſo much ſame might perceiued ſoone moore knowledge catuall concerning preſent captaine generall would haue ſent ye king would conſent therevnto moore tooke occaſion go ye generalls lodging fained friendſhip offering themſelues inſtruct ſhould beſt doethe fained friendſhippe more talking ſayd country accuſtomed thoſe came place buſineſſe king ſhoulde bring preſent therefore good hée ſende one captaine generall béeing offended iniurye hadde offered catuall king factour would conſent therevnto vpon yet thought beſt tarry till next daye afternoone came whome ſhewed himſelfe offended long tarrieng aunſwere touching matter nothing talked thing ſo went court king ſomewhat chaunged haue ſaid againſt captaine generall commaund come preſence thrée houres comming courſie commaundement giuen ther ſhould come embaſſadour two owne men offended y• thought ſame ſeperating men meant well therfore carry fernan martines one diego dia ſhe secretary come king receiue ſo well firſt time ſaid vnto ſeuere countenaunce tarried day came captaine generall aunſwered deferre comming found himſelfe weary reſon long way loath tell cauſe ſtaid woulde giue king occaſion talke preſent would haue ſent well appeare catuall factor would haue hindred ſending ſame vnto king yt well knew would haue made ſmall account thereof alſo muſt force haue told ſeene ſame neuertheleſſe coulde excuſed king ſpake vnto captaine generall thereof immediately ſaiengthe king quarrelleth vvith captaine generall tolde belonging great rich king yet brought preſent embaſſage friendſhip onelye therefore could tell friendſhip woulde haue ſince ſend nothing vnto captaine generall aunſwere maruel bring nothing came aſſuraunce ſhould méete ſince hath ſéene ſhould well perceiue king maſter héereafter ſende ſo god wil giue leaue carry newes diſcouery ſo giue credite letter hée bring ſhall ſée king doeth ſend word king ſtéede demaunding letter aſked whether king maſter ſende diſcouer ſtones men ſo ſend diſcouer men doth chaunce hée ſent preſent ſince manifeſt hée brought nothing ſayd told sanctum maria golde requeſting ſame captaine generall partly aſhamed ſée king ſo altered brought preſent moreouer demaund without honeſtie image aunſwered sanctum maria tolde made woode gylded ouer maſſie golde although yet would depart therewith forſomuch ſame preſerued sea brought ſame countrey king reply vpon anſwere demaunded thoſe letter king ſent whereof one portingale tongue arabian language theſe tolde ſent order king captaine generall tolde catuall hée would goe village vntill men come tarried houſe wherein reſted himſelfe raine howbeit came vntill almoſt sunne ſet ſo long tarry becauſe loſt waye come captine generall tolde time leaue whereas ſo hadde come ſooner hée hadde bene shippe wherevppon immediatelye hée demaunde catuall boate pinnace goe aboorde hée pretended thing aunſwered verye late ſhippes ride farre going night might miſſe therfore great deale better tarie vntill ye next day ye captaine generall made plaine anſwere ſo would giue almadias pinnace woulde immediatly returne king complain vpon forſomuch king ſent ſhips would ſéeme ſtay ill done ſince chriſtian ſpoken ſuch coulour wold haue returned calicut diſſimulation ye catuall catuall diſſemble make countenance though would giue thirtie almadias woulde haue ſo many howbeit tolde counſell beſt remaine ſo would goe contented therewith thus one parte ſent ſéeke almadias pinnace part commaunded owner ſame hide themſelues way becauſe ſhuld deliuer ſame meane ſeaſon went ſéeke thoſe pinnace captaine generall went along water ſide euill ſuſpition dealing done calicut commaunded gonſallo peres marriner two men go faſt could leaſerly prouide boat night drew ſo thrée houres within night ere coulde heare thing hée done alſo tarrye comming thoſe went nicholas coello captaine generall willinger ſtay night catuall placed within ſame ſundry nayres weapon ſo men ſhould goe forth appointed many enmyes withſtand neuertheleſſe god pleaſure catuall durſt venture kill captaine generall yet men moore hadde bribed great ſumme appeare captaine general would commaund shippes bée brought anye néerer alſo ſame ſo appareaunt vnto others men gaue counſaile deale therein catuall ſéeing would commaunde thoſe shippes bée brought néere ſhoare cauſe ſtaye offer wrong ſéeing hée could kill beginne requeſt bring sailes rudder shippes lande captaine generall beganne laugh ſayeng would neither doe one yet ſince king giue frée licenſe goe without condition therefore hée willed doe would iniuryes hée offered king ſhoulde bée made priuie knewe woulde doe iuſtice yet hée remayned ſome feare ſuſpect although outwardly ſhew ſame length captaine generall reſt feigning themſelues hungredthe general vneffectuall excuſe vnprouided victualls requeſt ſome men might goe prouide ſame hée woulde remaine alone catuall woulde agrée therevnto nowe men béeing feare ſée themſelues ſuch daunger came gonſallo peres ſuppoſing captaine generall ben liberty tarrieng others tolde hée hadde mette nicholas coello others tarryed theyr boates lande newes brought captaine generall hée afeard leaſt catuall ſhould know thereof knowne indéed would haue ſent pinnace many men themgonſallo peres ſent back ſhips haue taken therefore procure meanes could gonſallo peres ſhoulde ſecretlye returne thence vnto ſhippes put themſelues good order alſo ſhould goe informe caſe doth remaine nicholas coello hauing receiued diſpatch forthwith depart brother bring ſhippes néere lande could perſwade captaine generall ſo doe ſaieng ſhould doe yet brother would conſent therevnto although would yet knew companye would catuall replye ſhoulde make merchaundiſe lande vntill ſuch time hée heard newes ſame ſolde neyther yet would goe anye lande becauſe hée would runne ſuch daunger moore grieuouſly offended thought ſo would come land might doe hurte seaboorde woulde rather ſo beganne make mocke merchandiſe left land alſo wrought mean could hinder ſales therof ſaieng yt wer litle nothing worth al ye captain general informeddeuiſes more captaine generall might ſend thoſe malabars detained whoſe wiues made exclamation impriſonment huſbands therefore king willinger ſet men libertie afterward remained king factor houſe ¶how captaine generall ſeeing delayes wer made factor scriuenor came bring himſelfe readines though would depart immediately wherevpon without delay king ſent away el happened chap 23 captain general ſéeing yt came determined proue whether yt ſhewing himſelf though wold depart immediatly wold thē ſend therfore wedneſday xxiii auguſt commaund wey ankor bring himſelfe vnder ſaile winde contrary driuen come ankor foure league calicut riding open road remained till next saterday ſée whether would ſende priſoners perceiuing likelihood thereof went yet sea ſo far ſcarcely could deſcry land ankor lack winde came thether boat wt certain malabars told ye captaine generall yt comming ſéeke tel y• diego dia ye others wer ye king pallaice minded ſend aboordyet 〈◊〉 deuices ſlaye portingals departing thing true would bind thēſelues yt ye next day ſhould brought ye cauſe brought thē thought ſhuld ouertake yt ſawe yt malabars yt generall kept priſoners thought yt dead craftie dealing purpoſe dally ye captaine general ſtay thoſe word king might meane prepare calicut armie ſhips ſet vpon tarry ſhips meca ioyne fléete captaine generall commaunded thoſe towne goe way retourne without men el letter ſo would ſink wt ordinance alſo immediately returne anſwere yt would cut head thoſe taken aunſwere thoſe towne departe immediatelye ſoone winde made ſayle bearing along coaſt came ankor sunne ſet ouer againſt calycut next daye men deſcryed comming ſeauen almadias came aboord captaine generalls ſhip one whereof came diego dia aluoro de braga others came many others countrey howbeit none durſt enter within ſhips put diego dia aluoro de braga owne boate ſtearne afterwarde themſelues fell tarrieng captaine generalls aunſwere diego dia ſaid ſoone king calicut knew gone ſent factor houſe ſhewed himſelfe ioyfull one knew nothing impriſonment aſked occaſion captaine generall tooke thoſe men doth kéepe priſoners afterward tolde cauſe wherevpon king made aunſwere well done aſked alſo whether factor demaunded hand thing gift ſpeaking againſt owne factor preſent knew wel inough yt long ago ſince cō maunded one killed taking certain bribe merchaunt ſcraungers willed tell captaine generall ſhould ſend ye ſtone promiſed ſet countrey vpon croſſe royall armes portingale alſo know whether content leaue diego dia factor calicut ſame ſent letter king portingale confirmed ſigned king written diego dia letter ſent aluoro de braga captaine generall tooke letter written certaine leafe palme trée vpon doe vſe write matter ſhall indure long time effect whereof vaſco de la gama gentleman thy houſe came countriethe effect ye king calicuts letter whoſe comming glad countrie great ſtore cinamon cloaues pepper precious ſtones deſirous haue thy countrie siluer gold corall skarlet captaine generall ſawe king vſe truth woulde aunſwere offer therewith ſent ſuch hadde ſtayed nayres others ſent word would ſend vntill ſuch time ſent ſuch merchaundiſe taken notwithſtanding hée ſent ſtone ſent anſwere departed thoſe brought diego dyas aboord next day came boord bontaybo tolde captaine generall came ſo ſodeinly away calicut catuall king commaundement taken euer ſaieng chriſtian comming calicut ouer land king portingales commaundement onely bée ſpie matter told ſame came moore procurement knew wel tooke good ſo meant ſome ſhrewd turne perſon ſo bée coulde haue taken therefore came way captaine generall glad comming tolde hée would carry portingale ſhuld recouer good doublebontaibo vvilling goe portingal beſides reward king maiſter would giue commaunded alſo ſhip ſhould prepared principall good cabine tenne clocke came boorde captaine generall thrée pinnace laden men vpon certeine ſeates bench layd certeine skarfs ſhould ſay came part theyr merchaundiſe theſe came foure one another touching thoſe thrée brought thoſe skarfes tolde captaine generall came theyr merchandiſe would put boate therefore willed bring thether thoſe malabars priſoners woulde fetch captaine generall perceiuing fetche goe waye hée woulde haue none theyr merchaundiſe thoſe malabars carrye portingale witneſſes diſcouerie ſo god diuine goodneſſe doe giue lyfe hée woulde ſhortly retourne calicut ſhoulde well knowe whether thoſe chriſtians théeues moore hadde made king calycut beléeue therefore cauſe hée ſo manifeſt wrong béeing done hée commaunded ſhoote many péeces ordinaunce feare thereof ranne theyr waye ſo hée king ſhippes bene readyneſſe floate ſent againſt captanie generall haled vp becauſe winter bée beléeued haue béene handye worke god shippes ſhoulde bée ſeaſon might eſcape carrye newes diſcouerye countrye reſtore ſame holye catholike faith otherwiſe ben summer woulde haue hadde fléete readineſſe great ſo haue taken v meanes hadde bene none lefte haue carryed newes portingale departure captaine generall calycut towarde portingale happened vnto iland anſandina cap 22 although captaine generall reioyſed much hée diſcouered calicut yet fully ſatiſfied therwith altogether king conceiued againſt great diſpleaſure meanes iudged next fléet king maiſter ſhould ſend would run great daunger howbeit perceiuing lay power therfore contented onely diſcouery haue knowne india nauigation commodious countrie haue brought thence example ſpices drug precious ſtones alſo thinges within ſame citie hauing doe departed carrieng thoſe malabars taken hoped haue ſome agréement made king calicut returne anye fléet thurſday departure ralme league calicut came towarde ye number lx tonys full souldiers king calicut thought haue taken ſéeing comming commaunded ordinaunce ſhot oftentimes done ſo would haue put greate daunger followed houre halfe reaſon ſhowre raine came vpon ſodeine captaine generall driuen ſea boord fléete meane enimies fledde waye bearing courſe towards mylinde great calmes along coaſt thought good conuenient although ye king calicut abuſed ſundry way neceſſitie y• thoſe ſhould returne calicut ſhould haue friendſhip fauour receiue thence theyr lading spice vſe ſome friendſhip ſince king would gladde thereof eſpeciall exalted therefore write vnto letter arabian tongue penned language bontaybo craue pardon carrieng awaye thoſe malabars done intent ſhoulde witneſſes diſcouered hée ſent worde lefte factorie calycut ſorrie feare leaſt moore ſhoulde kill alſo occaſion often time land yet leaue woulde bée alwayes commaundement ſince king maiſter would gladde friendſhippe alſo foorthwith woulde ſende fléete greate abundaunce ſuch merchaundiſe doth demaund trade hence forth hée ſhoulde haue portingales citie would redound vnto great profit letter deliuered vnto one malabars carry ſame land place cōmāded deliuered afterward knew yt ſame deliuered ye king calicut ye captaine general going forward courſe along coaſt next thurſday fell amongſt certeine rock fléete one inhabited came forth ſundry pinnace men within ſame ſell fiſh victualls captaine generall receiue curteouſly commaunded giue ſhirts thing verye gladde wherevpon tooke occaſion aſke whether woulde content ſhoulde erected marke croſſe ſame royall armes portingale token portingals theyr friend aunſwered contented thereby well knew chriſtians ſo marke placed ſince time called el padron de sanctum maria day foreſaid name rocke called hence ſoone night drew winde began blow ſhoare captaine generall made ſaile kéeping alwayes along coaſte thurſdaie béeing 19 september hée fell goodly high lande harde ſame laye ſixe little ilandes came ankor going lande take water finde young man demaund concerning captaine generall whether moore chriſtian aunſwered hée chriſtian thought feare leaſt ſhould haue killed forſomuch place chriſtians young man carrie men within certeine riuer ſhewed moſt excellent water iſſued betwéene certeine rock ſo paine gaue red night cap next morning following came land foure others ſmall boate boord captaine generall brought ſell many gourd cowcombers wer demaunded generall whether countrie cinamon pepper aunſwered nothing cinamon deſirous ſée ſamecinamon grovving ſent two men return brought wt two gréene bough certeine trées doe take ſame reporting thereof great groue howbeit ſame wilde retourne came 20 countrie men brought ſell hen gourd cowes milke alſo requeſted captaine generall ſend certeine men ſhortly ſhould retourne greate ſtore drie cinamon hogges hennes great offer would let none men goe hée feared leaſt ſame ſome treaſon next daye dinner men going lande cut woode ſomewhat farre place fell ſoddeine vppon two boates laye harde ſhoare ſide captaine generall woulde immediatlye procure knowe till dinner thought know ſame redineſſe depart firſt commaund one marriners go vp top ſée whether could diſcry veſſels ſea boord tolde ſight eight great ſhips wer incalmed newes left going ſée others put himſelfe readineſſe winde ſuch ſort might ſerue came within two league fléete captaine generall made toward enimies perceiuing immediatly flye toward ſhoare▪ bearing ſorte broken rudder one ſame reaſon whereof thoſe within ſhip forced go boat toward lande nicholas coello next ſhip went immediatly layde ſame aboord thinking indéede finde ſome greate ſhore rich howbeit nothing el coco melaſus certeine kinde sugar made palmes date trées alſo founde therein manye bowes arrowes ſwoordes ſpeares targats ſeauen ranne themſelues ground men could come néere vnto ſhips followed boat thence beate ordinaunce ſo enimyes driuen leaue ſhippes béeing yet next day ankor came vnto ſeauen men country almadias tolde thoſe eight ſhips calicut king ſent take thoſe fled away vnderſtood captaine generall went anſandina take water alſo toke moore priſoner ſeruant lord iland goa called sabayo taken ſpie cap 25 captaine generall thus informed would tarrie longer immediatlye came ankor ilande anſandina diſtaunt thence two gunne ſhotte tolde excellent ſwéete water iland little league firme land ſame many wood alſo two conduit head made frée ſtone excellent ſweete water ſprings riſe ther wherof one ſixe foote déepe alſo ſea ſayde iland great ſtore fiſh moore vſe traficke india ſame inhabited gentilesanſādina forſaken inhabitant goodly building eſpeciall pagodes goodly thing moore came red ſea began ſaile way reſorted thether alwayes take water wood ſo abuſe inhabitant could wel abide ſame ſo left dwelling ther going away plucked downe almoſt pagods▪ ſo left nothing ſtanding verye chappell lyke building yet theſe gentile wer firme land belong king narſingas pagode ſuch deuotion thence would goe ſundry time make ſame praiers vnto thrée black ſtones lieng middeſt ſaid chappell iland called anſandina malabars language called • iue ilandes rounde ſame lye foure captaine generall hauing come ankor ſent nicholas coello companye diſcouer ſame founde according afore declared goodlye place grounde might newe graue ſhips captaine generall great courſe run alſo knew finde ſo conuenient place conſulted captaines bring ſhippes ground firſt ſhip brought groundethey repaire ſhips shippe called ber •• whileſt thus occupyed came many people ſell victualls time came two ſmall brickentines hadde theyr standerds flagges toppes theyr maſtes within theyr trumpettes drumnies wherevppon came playeng theyr pleaſure theſe brickentines came manye men oare along ſhoare ſide fiue came ſuccour ſhoulde haue anye néede captaine generall hée hadde fight warning giuen malabars beware rouers vnder couloure peace robbe coulde take hée entered ſhippe hée perceiued hée might haue taken ſo bée hée woulde haue conſented lette come aboorde hée woulde agrée ſame therefore ſoone came within gunne ſhotte commaunded theyr ordinaunce ſhot thoſe two ſhippes floate fearing ſhotte gaue lowde voice crieng tambarane tambarane ſo doe call god often ſhooting fledde theyr way nicholas coello béeing boate went alwayes ſhooting ordinaunce purſued ſo farre captaine generall driuen put vp flagge ſigne hée ſhoulde retourne ſo next daye captaine generall men béeing land working vpon ſhip called berrio came two litle paraos number twelue men countrie apparel ſéemed bée ſome countenauncesugar cane grovving brought preſent bundell sugar cane immediately ſoone deliuered ſame aſked licenſe goe aboord ſée ſhips neuer ſaw captaine generall greatly offended requeſt feared leaſt ſpies whileſt talke came thether two paraos many men thoſe came firſt ſéeing captaine generall ſomewhat growen cholar thoſe came afterward come lande returne againe ſhip berrio made redineſſe afterward generalls ſhip brought ground new rigged hauing lande hir captaines came man little parao ſéemed age fortie yeares countrey vpon sabaco fine cotten reached downe héeles head toocke towell alſo couered part face gyrdell faw •• skeyne aſſoone leapt lande went immediately imbrace captaine generall one ſéene knowen ſelfe ſame ſort vſed captaines telling chriſtian borne italy hée brought countrey childe dwelling noble man moore called sabayo lord certaine iland called goa lieng twelue league thence forty thouſand horſemen within ſayd iland habitation amongſt moore obſerued lawe howbeit outward ſhew inwardly ſoule chriſtian sabayos houſe tolde come sea calycut certaine men ſhips whereof neuer ſéene ye like india none vnderſtoode language alſo body couered ouer cloathes vnderſtanding ſame immediatelye iudged frangnes ſo call thoſe chriſtians countrey deſirous ſée therefore aſked lycenſe sabayo ſaieng ſo woulde giue licenſe goe ſée knewe verye well ſhould dye thought anger reaſon whereof gaue licenſe whome hée ſent word ſo countrey anye thing yt néede ſhuld haue ſame eſpeciall ſhippes victualles moreouer woulde come dwell countrey would gladde thereof would giue ſufficient lyuing ſhould liue honourably ended thus talke captaine generall aſked perticularly countrey sabayo thing wherevppon requeſted captaine generall chéefe ſende companion remained firme lande agréed betwéene ſo well entertained woulde ſende vnto token ſigne thereof kinde dealing made captaine generall ſuſpect notwithſtanding commaunded chéefe giuen alſo two newe loaues ſent companion aforeſaide remained alwayes talking captaine generall talke ſo much ſome time hée diſcouered himſelfe bée ſpye paulo de la gama noted ſame aſked certaine countrey men hée vp tolde rouer laide aboorde shippes bene brought grounde time captaine generall béeing thereof informed commaunded carried aboorde ſhippe grounde commaunded bee well whipped confeſſe whether anye parte ſame true hée tolde alſo meant comming thether whether moore chriſtian aunſwered chriſtian ſaid al reſt denied therefore general ſought one cruell torment whipping hanging vp member pulley hoiſt vp downe great paine ſuffered requeſted let downe would tell trutha notable coūterfait diſcouered come downe declared hée ſpie ſent thether diſcouer manye men captaine generall weapon forſomuch ill beloued along coaſt becauſe chriſtiana kinde boates ſo called manyr atalayas foyſts placed euery baye kricke ſet vpon howbeit durſt vntill ſuch time came thether fortie great veſſells making readineſſe ioyne thoſe armed ſo ſet vpon take therefore meane ſpace ſent knowe ſayd affirmed alſo knewe certainelye thoſe fortie ſayle woulde come much declared receiued thrée foure torment reſt vnderſtood coniectures forſomuch perticularlye declare ſame captaine generall ſéeing would declare contented aduice giuen commaunded priſon vnder hatch carrie vnto portingale alſo cured verye well giue ſome refreſhing victualles afterward tolde minde kéepe priſoner haue captiue carie vnto king maſter ende might tell ſome newes india knowing verye well would rewarde captaine generall hauing knowledge comming enimies would therefore tarrie longer whileſt ſhip new dreſſing done ten dayes inſtaunt captaine generall offered ſhippe ſhippe taken eight ſet vpon thouſand fanons wold take ſaieng wold ſell thing yt enimies commaunded ſame burnt captaine generalls ſhip ready water taken hée immediately departed vpon fifth daye october going sea boord two hundred league thaf iland moore caried priſoner ſeeing remedie ſaid would tell truth indéede dwell sabayo word brought captain generall went wandring vpon sea one knewe therefore preparing great fléete take sabayo hauing notice thereof commaunded goe thether viſite marke went alſo ſée whether hée could bring goa ſo could bring paſſe would laye hand vpon fame went valyaunt ſo meant kéepe make warres againſt king next neighbour theſe newes captaine generall glad heare gaue thenceforth better entertainment allowed apparell alſo money afterward made chriſtian gaue name gaſpar moore chriſtened honour one thrée king called magus name captaine generall god father gaue title ſurname ſo euer called gaſpar de la gamas ¶how captaine generall went forwarde voyage towarde mylynde great trouble paſt vntill ſuch time came thether chap 26 following hence courſe towards mylynde whether hee minded returne take embaſſadour went alwayes cruell ſtormes captaine generall continually indured vntil ſuch time entred goulfe hauing alwayes winde right againſt occaſion ſhippes made ſmall way therefore longer time entered gulfe entered within ſame troubled great calmes sea troubleſome gouerning ſhips alſo heat hurtfull vpon ſea vpon land ther couering defend sunnemen ſtifled vvith sunne onely whereon ſame men ſtiffeled vp hath bene ſéene voyage toward india ſay winde hauing courſing thus heates ſpace many dayes together afterward returne breake vp contrary windes go forward good goe backward captaine generall loath go backward wold yet rather tarie ther wher indéed perceiued winde ſo great sea went ſo high tarrieng ſhippes driuen force kéepe sea ſometime boord ſometime ſo men paſſed great trouble reaſon inough doe gouerne ſhips hoping ſo great ſtormes would come faire weather driuen pray thoſe great calmes ſawe weather like endure many dayes water beganne fayle occaſion captaine generall commaunded ſame deliuered order going neceſſitie alſo fowle weather people began fall ſicke diſeaſe gum riuer de buenas sennal • went calicut skurfe alſo armes leg ſwell beſides ſwellings riſe bodyes reaſon peſtilent ſtinking humour caſt laſke new infirmitie dyed number thirtie perſons began die continued kinde weather vppon sea ther aroſe ſuch feare amongſt thoſe remain aliue fared ſame men amazed beléeued verely ſhould neuer goe thence thought kinde weather alwayes durable ſame cauſe indured ſo long maſters pilot fléete lyke opinion made reſt beléeue ſooner meanes crye thoſe well ſicke great ſaieng ſince weather would ſerue goe thence yet requeſted occaſion death rather conſent retourne vnto calycut el ſome place india béeing ther receiue god ſhuld appoint rather dye thoſe ſeas terrible diſeaſes ther likelihoode remedie eſpeciall hauing lacke thing victual water began want reaſon long continuaunce ſaid place ſpent captaine generall ſéeing great feare men animate ſayd vnto ſorte requeſting content beléeue ſuch weather courſed ſorte alwayes lyke continue ſo bée ſo woulde nauigation goulph strayghtes meca mylynde yet anye place ſhoulde paſſe vnpoſſible might ſomewhat digreſſe right courſe therefore met theſe calmes windes indured yet thoſe ſaide ſhould haue ende ſame trouble lykewiſe ende marriners woulde beléeue trouble continued foure monethes alſo dead theyr fellowes thirtie perſons ſo ſo fewe remayninga vvofull mortalitie euery ſhip ſixtéene perſons left gouerne ſame ſome verye ſicke diſeaſe aboue ſayde meanes fell ſuch deſperation reaſon thought ſhoulde goe doe affirme paulo de la gama nicholas coello béeing captaines made agréement theyr shippes ſo bée woulde come anye winde might retourne india woulde ſurelye doe ſo béeing thus determined vppon ſodayne came freſh gale winde fléete might goe forwarde ſame ſixteene dayes came within ſight lande béeing wedneſday ſeconde februarye marriners reioyced ſuch ſort meanes ſame forgotten theyr trouble daungers paſt gaue vnto god great thankes gracious benefites hadde ſight lande founde themſelues ſo néere vnto captaine generall gaue commaundement caſt sea ſo much might bée thought ſufficient ſtaye vntill morning béeing come went foorthwith reknowledge lande ſée none knewe ſame although one moore ſayde hadde taken theyr courſe directlye towardes monſanbique ſtandeth betwéene certaine ilandes ſtanding ouer againſt thrée hundred league ſhore whereas people ſame countrey continually ſicke ſame diſeaſe men morning come went reknowledge land came goodly great citie walled round within ſame faire high houſes midſt ſame great pallaice ſtood high ſéemed goodly building ſaw well ſhips citie called magadoxo citie magadoxo ſtandeth ende ſaid goulfe coaſt aethiopia hundred thirtéene league mylynde ſcituation whereof ſhall declare héereafter captaine generall knew ſame bée citie moore hée went along coaſt hée commaunded ſhoote manye péeces ordinaunce alſo coulde tell farre hée mylynde thence forward ſtayed night becauſe would paſſe ſame foorthwith saturday fifth februarie lieng ouer againſt village moore call pate hundred thrée league magadoxo came thence eight terradas certaine kinde boates countrey full souldiours made theyr waye ſtraight towarde fléete fromwhence ſhot ſo many péeces ordinaunce thought themſelues happy haue eſcaped running awaye howbeit men followe lacke winde next mundaye following generall arriued mylynde béeing king ſent viſite captaine generall ſundrye freſh victualls ſending word alſo glad hée comming generall aunſwered againe fernan martines whome hée ſent preſent becauſe thoſe ſicke whome hée deſirous haue cured hée tarryed fiue dayes time died many preſent king licenſe cauſed ſet land marke token friendſhip prouided himſelfe victual departed wedneſday morning béeing xvii februarie embaſſadour whome king captaine generall men inough gouerne whole fléete thought good aduiſe captaines burne one thoſe ſhippes ſame ſhould saint raphael determined doe rather forſomuch ſame al open brought grounde others therof would doe nothing feare hée minded doe ſhould vpon requeſt ſo aunſwered letter haue ſéene thy meſſagethe king cochings anſvvere reply ſoundeth threatenings god alwaies reſiſteth pride doth greatlye bound giue thée ſame ſo appeareth doe feede thy humour councell thée according thy ſince thou art deſirous accept according good reaſon thou haſt leaue ſo bée without flatterye thou without paſſion wouldeſt iudge weigh cauſe theſe chriſtians thou ſhouldeſt finde vnto preſent time haue giuen thée cauſe ſhould well receiued thy countrie ſo prouince malabar hunt foorth lyke théeues cannot bée called although preſent foraſmuch place worlde men doe reſorte hether aſſemble themſelues buye thoſe merchaundiſe haue theyr countryes bring thoſe hether haue héere ſame ſorte come theſe chriſtians cuſtome merchauntes brought thée king behalfe richeſt preſent thou diddeſt yet euer receiue beſides theyr merchandiſe brought much golde ſiluer made coine doe vſe bring come make warres ſo bée hadde come anye ſuch ſorte woulde haue diſſimuled running awaye pleadges offered vnto whome thou doeſt call embaſſadours kepte priſon theyr captaine lande reconciling themſelues vnto thée went tooke ſhippe thy requeſt greate elephant afterward preſent thée therwith ſame ſhip carried beſides thoſe théeues doe vſe ſo doe yet paye ſo well vſe ſo much truth time calycut none complaine onely moore enimies mooued enuy ſée pertakers profite accuſe hadde taken greate ſtore pepper owner againſt theyr will themſelues béeing thoſe vſe ſame chriſtians ſhoulde benefite themſelues lading theyr ſhips foraſmuch ſo apparant thou gaueſt licenſe take theyr fraight licenſe captaine ſent ſhippe moore laden béeing whole fault yet notwithſtanding riſe againſt theſe men haue done well knowne world yet quiet men ought doe tarryed one daye ſée whether thou woldeſt excuſe thy ſelfe ſéeing came none thée put execution reuengethe execution ye pledge defended king brother traiterouſly moore doe went defend ſhips although ſpeake ſtout ſtomacke councell thée make theſe warres againſt king coching receiue citie iuſt cauſe receiuing iudged hinder thée receiued would anye merchaunt would haue come ſtomacke ſo lyberally king well taken one reſpect valyaunt gentleman another great credit authoritie cauſe hadde great reputation inſomuch moore caymayles ſhewed themſelues verye ſtout againſt king bene great deale better captain done haue left alone ſame runne daunger méete ſeas ſo great fléet king calicut ſet vpon mée ſo ſhould haue remained haue done ſo foule déede yet would haue tolde thée thereof ſo meant doe afearde king calycuts power doe take thée man indued reaſon ſuppoſe thou wouldeſt haue thought ill thereof otherwiſe thoſe béeing warned thereof might haue bene profitable vnto thée haue remained frée enuie mallice king calicut thing ſo moore conſidered would haue tolde thée ſo great fable beleeue could haue done thée greater iniurie would haue done good thou doeſt beare vnto v doe knowe well let trouble thée although thou doeſt looſe reſt thy ſubiectes yet thou doeſt recouer many portingales héere remaine die thy ſeruice néede onely cauſe wée remaine india eſpecially man bound therevnto ſo y• wold fidelitye truth thou haſt alwaies vſed towards men vntill ſuch time thou diddeſt looſe coching diddeſt ſée ſame burnt cauſe thou oughteſt eſtéeme better thy ſelfe thereby thou haſt exalted thy fame countrie therfore thy name wil remaine euer greateſt treaſure king canne leaue behinde onely thing men doe ſéeke beléeue king calycut firſt ſet fire coching ſame béeing theyr caruell theyr boates coulde ſcarcelye bée diſcerned fléete occupyed almoſt paſſage meanes rope gaue one rope wounde cheynes ſhould cut ſunder hadde done commaundement giuen giue fire valiantly men defended themſelues battell went great heate ordinaunce went ſo often lykewiſe ſmall ſhot none coulde ſee one another ſmoake ſame caruell boates ſo flame fire ſo cruelly handle enimyes eightéene ſunke thirtéene fledde awaye reſidue gaue place enimyes greate number ſlaine hurt came vize admerall called lord repelyn another ſquadron gaue proud onſet ſo king calycut giue lyke vpon land battaile farre vehement firſt manye enimyes ſlaine appeared water coulour bloud yet lorde repelyn made lowde outeryes commaunding laye caruell aboorde durſt venture doe rather deſirous goe theyr waye chriſtian prince yt might know thoſe notable act victory ſuch thing within theſe dayes prince hath done ye like ſubiects finis ❧imprinted london thomas eaſt dwelling betweene paules wharſe baynards
